# Firefox Content Security Policy Enforcement Audit

## Your Task

Audit the Content Security Policy (CSP) enforcement infrastructure in Firefox. Find all C++ source files in `mozilla-firefox/firefox` under `dom/security/` that implement CSP parsing, evaluation, and violation reporting. Specifically: 1. The file that defines `nsCSPParser` — the CSP directive parser. 2. The file that implements `nsCSPContext` — the main CSP context that holds policies. 3. The file that implements CSP violation reporting (`nsCSPUtils` or similar). 4. The header file that declares the `nsIContentSecurityPolicy` XPCOM interface. 5. The file under `dom/security/` that performs script-src evaluation for inline scripts. Report each file path and its primary class or function.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the compliance domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've completed the audit of the Content Security Policy (CSP) enforcement infrastructure in Firefox. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

### Files Located in `dom/security/`:

1. **nsCSPParser** (`nsCSPParser.h`/`.cpp`)
   - Parses CSP directives from policy strings
   - Implements `parseContentSecurityPolicy()` function
   - Tokenizes and validates policy grammar

2. **nsCSPContext** (`nsCSPContext.h`/`.cpp`)
   - Main CSP context implementing the `nsIContentSecurityPolicy` XPCOM interface
   - Holds and enforces multiple policies
   - Implements `GetAllowsInline()` for inline script/style checking
   - Implements `ReportInlineViolation()` for violation reporting

3. **nsCSPUtils** (`nsCSPUtils.h`/`.cpp`)
   - Utility classes: `nsCSPDirective`, `nsCSPScriptSrcDirective`, `nsCSPStyleSrcDirective`
   - `nsCSPScriptSrcDirective` specifically handles script-src evaluation for inline scripts
   - Implements nonce, hash, and keyword (e.g., `unsafe-inline`) checking
   - Provides violation reporting constants and helper functions

4. **XPCOM Interface** (`dom/interfaces/security/nsIContentSecurityPolicy.idl`)
   - Declares the public XPCOM interface with CSPDirective enums
   - Defines interface methods for CSP checking and policy management

5. **CSPEvalChecker** (`CSPEvalChecker.h`/`.cpp`)
   - Performs eval() restriction checking
   - Methods: `CheckForWindow()` and `CheckForWorker()`
   - Enforces script-src `unsafe-eval` restrictions

6. **CSPViolationData** (`CSPViolationData.h`/`.cpp`)
   - Represents CSP violation data structure
   - Tracks blocked content source, directives, and source location

The parseContentSecurityPolicy() static method tokenizes and parses the policy string according to CSP grammar specifications.\\n\\n2. **Main CSP Context**: The nsCSPContext class (dom/security/nsCSPContext.h and nsCSPContext.cpp) implements the nsIContentSecurityPolicy XPCOM interface and serves as the primary container for CSP policies. It holds an array of nsCSPPolicy objects and is responsible for policy enforcement decisions through methods like ShouldLoad() for resource loads and GetAllowsInline() for inline script/style evaluation.\\n\\n3. **CSP Utilities and Directives**: The nsCSPUtils.h and nsCSPUtils.cpp files contain the core directive classes including nsCSPDirective (base class), nsCSPScriptSrcDirective (for script-src evaluation), and nsCSPStyleSrcDirective. The nsCSPScriptSrcDirective class specifically handles inline script allowance evaluation through its allows() and allowsAllInlineBehavior() methods. It also manages worker restrictions and script element/attribute restrictions.\\n\\n4. **XPCOM Interface Declaration**: The nsIContentSecurityPolicy.idl file (located at dom/interfaces/security/) declares the XPCOM interface with CSPDirective enums and methods for querying CSP allowances. This interface is implemented by nsCSPContext.\\n\\n5. **Inline Script Evaluation**: Script-src evaluation for inline scripts is performed through the nsCSPScriptSrcDirective class which evaluates against nonce, hash, and keyword sources (unsafe-inline, strict-dynamic). The GetAllowsInline() method in nsCSPContext checks directives like SCRIPT_SRC_ELEM_DIRECTIVE and SCRIPT_SRC_ATTR_DIRECTIVE for inline allowance.\\n\\n6. **Eval Checking**: The CSPEvalChecker class (dom/security/CSPEvalChecker.h and CSPEvalChecker.cpp) provides static methods CheckForWindow() and CheckForWorker() to verify whether eval() operations are permitted by the CSP, checking against the script-src directive's restriction on unsafe-eval.\\n\\n7. **Violation Reporting**: CSP violations are reported through ReportInlineViolation() and ReportViolation() methods in nsCSPContext, with violation details stored in CSPViolationData structures (dom/security/CSPViolationData.h and CSPViolationData.cpp) that capture blocked content source type, effective directive, source location, and optional script hash samples.\"\n}\n",
